<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_eee617f5-63a9-41fa-9807-0bbebd798c44'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14269424780296062770">When Eva's film star sister Katrina dies, she leaves California and returns to Cornwall, where they spent their childhood summers, to scatter Katrina's ashes and in doing so return her to the place where she belongs. But Eva must also confront the ghosts from her own past, as well as those from a time long before her own. For the house where she so often stayed as a child </span>
  <span id="freeText14269424780296062770" style="display:none">When Eva's film star sister Katrina dies, she leaves California and returns to Cornwall, where they spent their childhood summers, to scatter Katrina's ashes and in doing so return her to the place where she belongs. But Eva must also confront the ghosts from her own past, as well as those from a time long before her own. For the house where she so often stayed as a child is home not only to her old friends the Halletts, but also to the people who had lived there in the eighteenth century. When Eva finally accepts that she is able to slip between centuries and see and talk to the inhabitants from hundreds of years ago, she soon finds herself falling for Daniel Butler, a man who lived - and died - long before she herself was born. Eva begins to question her place in the present, and in laying her sister to rest, comes to realise that she too must decide where she really belongs, choosing between the life she knows and the past she feels so drawn towards.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14269424780296062770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Although her two most recent books (The Firebird and A Desperate Fortune) have stronger links to one or two of her earlier books, each of her novels can be read independent of the others.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

I cried again this time around, which is always a bonus feature :D<br/><br/><br/><br/><b>Original Review:</b><br/><br/><b>How does she do it?</b><br/><br/>No, seriously, how does Susanna Kearsley manage to engage me, move me to tears and surp</span>
  <span id="freeText7948385760595886952" style="display:none"><b>Re-read January, 2014 with Jeannette and Diane Lynn:</b><br /><br />Actually a better read the second time around, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[as I was able to watch for the myriad clues Kearsley had laid down throughout the storyline that culminated in her cool twist at the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Great story; warm and wonderful characters. I cried again this time around, which is always a bonus feature :D<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Original Review:</b><br /><br /><b>How does she do it?</b><br /><br />No, seriously, how does Susanna Kearsley manage to engage me, move me to tears and surprise me time and time again with her brillant writing skills? Frankly, I have no answers, except to say that Kearsley's stories speak directly to my heart in a way no other writer since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1040250.M_M__Kaye" title="M.M. Kaye" rel="nofollow noopener">M.M. Kaye</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart" title="Mary Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Stewart</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier" title="Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daphne DuMaurier</a> has done.<br /><br />The worlds she pens are grounded in the every day realities of modern life, but brushed with the magic of possibilities of lives redeemed, transformed, or made complete by the convergence or confluence of time slip or time travel. That meeting of past and present lives is full of historical adventure and romance, and usually offers the reader a nice surprise twist by the end (not to mention a few tears along the way).<br /><br />The emotional appeal and impact of <i>The Rose Garden</i> is further strengthened by the fact that the main character, Eva, has suffered the loss of her beloved sister at the beginning of the novel. Her coming to terms with that loss, and where she belongs in the world, is an ever present fixture throughout the book. Fans of Kearsley will know that she lost her own sister not long ago, so the feelings expressed and felt by Eva are no doubt culled in some part from the writer's own experience, and will certainly resonate with those of us who too have lost people we love.<br /><br />There are some minor quibbles I have that make the story less then a "perfect book": the love story (which read in places like a cheesy romance novel), the novel's pacing (which alternated between smoothly flowing and engaging to slow and boring, IMO - sorry!) the time travel aspects (which were pulled off fairly well, but it still wasn't possible to suspend disbelief 100% of the time) and the somewhat abrupt ending (could we not get a little epilogue or something??) However, as my 5 stars will attest, it was the "perfect book" for me, and certainly now becomes my second favorite Kearsley after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6171571.Mariana" title="Mariana by Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">Mariana</a>, which still holds top spot. <i>The Rose Garden</i> resonates with haunting passages reminiscent of du Maurier's novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5292251.Frenchman_s_Creek" title="Frenchman's Creek by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Frenchman's Creek</a>, lyrical place descriptions worthy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart" title="Mary Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Stewart</a>, and the hallmark emotional punch of Kearsley's own style, which is in a class all it's own.<br /><br /><br />Thank you, Susanna, for another winner! Now please write faster...</span>
  <a data-text-id="7948385760595886952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_453151122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453151122" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453151122?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12273538-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453151122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6246003750086279917"><br/>I find it difficult to rate this novel. On one hand, I was sufficiently engaged by the narrative and the characters to read it in two or three sittings. On the other hand, it requires a massive suspension of disbelief, which at times I found difficult to sustain. <br/><br/>The heroine is Eva Ward, who after the death of her much loved sister, travels from the United States to Cornwall to scatter her sister's ashes near Trelowarth House, where she and her sister spent their childhood summers. Family friend</span>
  <span id="freeText6246003750086279917" style="display:none"><br />I find it difficult to rate this novel. On one hand, I was sufficiently engaged by the narrative and the characters to read it in two or three sittings. On the other hand, it requires a massive suspension of disbelief, which at times I found difficult to sustain. <br /><br />The heroine is Eva Ward, who after the death of her much loved sister, travels from the United States to Cornwall to scatter her sister's ashes near Trelowarth House, where she and her sister spent their childhood summers. Family friends - rose grower Mark and his sister Susan - still live in the house and their artist stepmother Claire lives in a cottage on the estate. Eva inexplicably finds herself time-travelling back to Trelowarth House as it was in 1715, where she encounters the smuggling Butler brothers and their Irish friend Fergal O'Cleary and becomes caught up in an aspect of the 1715 Jacobite rebellion. The rebellion is the event around which the 1715 part of the narrative revolves, but it's not really the point of the novel. Rather, this is a romance between Eva and Daniel Butler, a couple separated by time.<br /><br />I'm not sure whether I like the novel because I have some (very distant) Cornish ancestry, because I've been to Cornwall and can picture the landscape in my head or because I love Daphne du Maurier's descriptive writing and I strongly feel the possibly unconscious influence of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84573.Frenchman_s_Creek" title="Frenchman's Creek by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Frenchman's Creek</a> on Kearsley's writing. It may be a combination of all of those factors. In addition, I like Kearsley's prose and her ability to describe landscape. <br /><br />However, even the strengths of the novel don't completely hide its weaknesses. One of them is Kearsley's attempt to provide scientific support for the idea of time travel. As I recall, she did the same thing with the concept of genetic memory in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3392089.The_Winter_Sea" title="The Winter Sea by Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winter Sea</a>. This is neither helpful nor necessary, particularly in the case of this novel, as Kearsley refers to Stephen Hawking in support of an assertion that time travel is possible. This is problematic because Hawking, as far as I know, believes that forward time travel may be possible, but not backward time travel. If you're writing a work of the imagination, then whether or not time travel is actually possible is beside the point and references to science only draw attention to the implausibility of the concept. And implausible it is, because in this novel time travel seems to happen randomly with no persuasive explanation for why it only happens to Eva <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and, as it happens, to one other character <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.*<br /><br />Speaking of implausible, something that really struck me was just how incurious those 18th century men seem to be. A young woman materialises in the house and announces she's from 300 years in the future and virtually the only reaction is "You're from the future? Right then, you'd best pop on this frock 'cos you look a bit funny and why don't you pretend you can't talk so that people don't notice your funny accent. Now, what'll we have for supper?" I think not. <br /><br />Another problem is the fact that not a lot actually happens. Eva is sad, she goes to Cornwall, she travels back and forward in time. She falls in love. When back in 1715, she's a woman, so she can't really do very much except wait around for things to happen. That said, there's a bit more action in the last quarter of the novel and a nice twist at the end, part of which I had anticipated, but elements of the twist still took me by surprise. <br /><br />I know that I'm being nit-picky about a book which I actually enjoyed reading. Overall, I would have preferred a little more depth and a little less fluff. But this does not pretend to be great literature. It's pure escapism and a pleasant way to spend a few hours. And it made me want to go back to Cornwall, which is no bad thing. This is in 3-1/2 star territory, but creeping up towards four. I liked it more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3392089.The_Winter_Sea" title="The Winter Sea by Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winter Sea</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/961836.Season_of_Storms" title="Season of Storms by Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">Season of Storms</a>, but not as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/65086.Every_Secret_Thing__Kate_Murray___1_" title="Every Secret Thing (Kate Murray, #1) by Emma Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Secret Thing</a>. I'm still waiting for the Kearsley novel which will blow me away. <br /><br />*An explanation of sorts is provided, but it's very weak.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6246003750086279917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161393630" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161393630" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3820197-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383385041p2/3820197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161393630?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/3820197-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402258589" href="/book/show/10836066-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820197-jill?shelf=romantic-historical-fiction">romantic-historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3820197-jill?shelf=2011-4-5-5-stars">2011-4-5-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161393630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15977602779468408642"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>'Whatever time we have,' he said, 'it will be time enough.'</i><br/><br/>When Eva Ward's sister dies she returns to Cornwall to scatter her ashes, to the place where they had spent their happy childhood summers, Trelowarth House. The gardens at Trelowarth have for generations grown roses and been tended by generations of Halletts, with Eva's friends Mark and his sister Susan Hallett now in charge of the house and gardens.<br/><br/>It is on her first morning there that Eva begins to experience a series of stran</span>
  <span id="freeText15977602779468408642" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>'Whatever time we have,' he said, 'it will be time enough.'</i><br /><br />When Eva Ward's sister dies she returns to Cornwall to scatter her ashes, to the place where they had spent their happy childhood summers, Trelowarth House. The gardens at Trelowarth have for generations grown roses and been tended by generations of Halletts, with Eva's friends Mark and his sister Susan Hallett now in charge of the house and gardens.<br /><br />It is on her first morning there that Eva begins to experience a series of strange events, voices and hallucinations that she puts down to grief and stress at the recent loss of her sister. But when these hallucinations continue and grow ever clearer, Eva realises that what she is experiencing is real, and that somehow she is able to move back and forth through time.<br /><br />In 1715, Daniel Butler is the resident of Trelowarth House with his brother Jack and his friend Fergal. Daniel is a free-trader, although the law calls him a smuggler. But Eva has landed in a dangerous era. The 1715 Jacobite Uprising was not restricted to Scotland. James Stuart had his supporters in Cornwall as well. And Daniel is caught up in the intrigue of the times. As Eva continues to travel between her own time and the past she becomes increasingly attracted to Daniel. But with no say over how or when she travels through time, Eva wonders how this will all end and if she could ever have a future with Daniel. In the past.<br /><br />Like Susanna Kearsley's other novels I've read, this story has a gothic feel, not darkly gothic but hauntingly beautiful. She brings the story alive incorporating details of 18th century life such as food and cooking, running a household, clothing, sailing; and setting her story around real historical figures who were instrumental in the Jacobite Uprising in Cornwall. <br /><br />Susanna Kearsley effortlessly draws all the threads of her story together at the end, weaving the sub-plots into an integrated whole. Characters, remarks, events that seem incidental to the story become important later on. There is something so masterful and yet deceptively simple about Susanna Kearsley's prose. Her writing is like the little black cocktail dress - simple, classic, elegant. When Eva tries to understand what is happening to her, Daniel explains -<br /><br /><i>'When I meet a wind I cannot fight,' he said, 'I can do naught but set my sails to let it take me where it will.'</i><br /><br />Beautifully crafted, Susanna Kearsley has written another romantic historical fiction as fine as 'Mariana' and 'The Winter Sea'. At the conclusion of 'The Rose Garden' I was left with a sense of deep satisfaction. This is romantic historical fiction at its best.<br /><br />4.5 stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15977602779468408642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_292452030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292452030" />
    <a title="Patricia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2154354-patricia"><img alt="Patricia" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292452030?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia" href="/user/show/2154354-patricia">Patricia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12273538-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292452030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4186859359004873078">To me, a good time travel yarn must possess a certain amount of plausibility. I found this vital element seriously lacking in "The Rose Garden." Daniel and Fergal should have been shocked by a woman from the future suddenly appearing out of thin air; e.g., they should have been questioning her about her strange appearance, what time period she came from, what it was like in the future; etc., etc. Instead, they're pretty much blasé about this mysterious phantom woman. Fergal is a little taken aba</span>
  <span id="freeText4186859359004873078" style="display:none">To me, a good time travel yarn must possess a certain amount of plausibility. I found this vital element seriously lacking in "The Rose Garden." Daniel and Fergal should have been shocked by a woman from the future suddenly appearing out of thin air; e.g., they should have been questioning her about her strange appearance, what time period she came from, what it was like in the future; etc., etc. Instead, they're pretty much blasé about this mysterious phantom woman. Fergal is a little taken aback at first but any misgivings he has are short lived. Before you know it, he's behaving like a mother hen towards this poor girl from the future. It seems the author attempts to explain this scenario by depicting Daniel and Fergus as "scientific types." Well, scientifically-minded or not, most people would be slightly freaked out by something like this happening. This scenario is not even remotely believable.<br /><br />Although I thought the writing was good and I enjoyed reading the descriptions of Cornwall, I thought the characters were flat and uninteresting, and I had to force myself to keep reading. This is the first book by Susanna Kearsley I've read. Not sure I'll venture to read "Winter Sea."</span>
  <a data-text-id="4186859359004873078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1122196720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1122196720" />
    <a title="Frances" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37439004-frances"><img alt="Frances" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419968891p2/37439004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1122196720?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frances" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frances" href="/user/show/37439004-frances">Frances</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1122196720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9895554742967347873">A Good Yarn<br/>The tale is a good yarn, primarily along the romantic side with touches of historical data incorporated throughout. The author provides a substantial amount of detail about the main characters which makes them all the more realistic. Although I found it a bit slow at the beginning, I soon began to enjoy the colourful characters and found it flowed along nicely. If you have never read a S. Kearsley’s book then I highly recommend “Mariana” as a first pick which was superb. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_231682226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231682226" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2837258-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255560321p2/2837258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231682226?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/2837258-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402258589" href="/book/show/10836066-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2837258-katherine?shelf=own-kindle">own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2837258-katherine?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2837258-katherine?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2837258-katherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2837258-katherine?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2837258-katherine?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231682226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3328712769786887527">I find it interesting that Susanna Kearsley's books are compared to works by Daphne du Maurier, Mary Stewart, and Diana Gabaldon, some of my favorite authors. Kearsley certainly has du Maurier's talent for sense of place and Stewart's mix of romance and suspense, however I'm not so sold on the Gabaldon comparison though both do deal with time-travel. Gabladon's books are dense and history-heavy (something I happen to love) and while this may be historical fiction it's of a much lighter variety. </span>
  <span id="freeText3328712769786887527" style="display:none">I find it interesting that Susanna Kearsley's books are compared to works by Daphne du Maurier, Mary Stewart, and Diana Gabaldon, some of my favorite authors. Kearsley certainly has du Maurier's talent for sense of place and Stewart's mix of romance and suspense, however I'm not so sold on the Gabaldon comparison though both do deal with time-travel. Gabladon's books are dense and history-heavy (something I happen to love) and while this may be historical fiction it's of a much lighter variety. <br /><br />This book is romantic with just enough suspense and explanation behind the time-travel to make it a thoroughly enjoyable and satisfying read. For me, it would have come in at 4 stars (being a bit light in the historical element with a few references that had me raising my eyebrows) except I <i>loved</i> the time-travel twist at the end--that pushed it almost to 5 stars. A perfect "escape" book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3328712769786887527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_177827943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177827943" />
    <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead"><img alt="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328667000p2/3039709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177827943?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead">Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12273538-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177827943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3686581161678373282">3.5 stars out of 5<br/><br/>I keep seeing it everywhere... <br/><br/><i>"If you enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_' title='Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Outlander</a>, you'll love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9792287.The_Rose_Garden' title='The Rose Garden by Susanna Kearsley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rose Garden</a>"</i> <br/><br/>Ok...me, me, me!!!<br/><br/>I loved Outlander and the entire Outlander series. So, that means I'll love this book right?<br/><br/>Wrong. I didn't LOVE it. I liked it. It was good but not outstanding (the way Outlander was). It was interesting but not interesting enough to warrant the comparison to Outlander.<br/><br/>Hold up, don't get me wrong here.<br/><br/>This book was good. I thought the beginning was excellent. I thought the </span>
  <span id="freeText3686581161678373282" style="display:none">3.5 stars out of 5<br /><br />I keep seeing it everywhere... <br /><br /><i>"If you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_" title="Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlander</a>, you'll love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9792287.The_Rose_Garden" title="The Rose Garden by Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose Garden</a>"</i> <br /><br />Ok...me, me, me!!!<br /><br />I loved Outlander and the entire Outlander series. So, that means I'll love this book right?<br /><br />Wrong. I didn't LOVE it. I liked it. It was good but not outstanding (the way Outlander was). It was interesting but not interesting enough to warrant the comparison to Outlander.<br /><br />Hold up, don't get me wrong here.<br /><br />This book was good. I thought the beginning was excellent. I thought the ending was satisfying. It was the middle that made the book just good but not great.<br /><br />My experience with Susanna Kearsley consists of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3392089.The_Winter_Sea" title="The Winter Sea by Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winter Sea</a> &amp; this book. Both books I absolutely adored at the beginning. Both books I loved the ending. Both books I almost stopped reading in the middle out of pure boredom. Notice a pattern? Yup, the author has a tendency to drag the middle portion of her books to the point of book-stopping-boredom. I've learned in my vast Kearsley reading experience to read through the boredom so that I can be rewarded with a fantastic ending. It would be nice if her books didn't bore me at all in the middle but I can't have everything!<br /><br />Ok. I’ve said a lot without saying one word about the actual story. (it’s a talent of mine)<br /><br />The Story-<br /><br />The story is actually really simple-<br /><br />Girl’s sister dies. Girl goes back “home” to scatter sister’s ashes. Girl time travels. Girl falls for guy back in time. What to do? What to do?<br /><br />That pretty much sums up the plot. What saves the simple plot is the characters. They are well written and even the minor characters are interesting.<br /><br />Overall-<br /><br />Good but not great. Definitely not Outlander. Good book to read in between books in the Outlander series!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3686581161678373282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1728134565" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1728134565" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5512657-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543780395p2/5512657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1728134565?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/5512657-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sara by: </span>
      Carolee
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728134565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15889463088982721682">The moment I realized this novel was set in Cornwall, I was halfway to loving it already. Then it had that du Maurier flavor, the atmosphere of Jamaica Inn and the mystery element, the historical setting and charming gentleman that put me in mind of Winston Graham’s Poldark, with the addition of a well-conceived and executed time-travel angle. What’s not to like? My only regret is that I let it languish on my bookshelf for over a year.<br/><br/><i>There was something about this remote western corner of Brita</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15889463088982721682" style="display:none">The moment I realized this novel was set in Cornwall, I was halfway to loving it already. Then it had that du Maurier flavor, the atmosphere of Jamaica Inn and the mystery element, the historical setting and charming gentleman that put me in mind of Winston Graham’s Poldark, with the addition of a well-conceived and executed time-travel angle. What’s not to like? My only regret is that I let it languish on my bookshelf for over a year.<br /><br /><i>There was something about this remote western corner of Britain that captured the soul and refused to let go, something ancient and wild in the moors and black cliffs and the voice of the sea that spoke always of something unseen and enchanted.</i><br /><br />I was so in the mood for this sweet romantic tale that swept me along and swept me away from my everyday world of problems and sorrows. Sometimes, somewhere else is just where we want to be, and today 17th Century England was just the right place for me and Daniel Butler was just the right man.<br /><br />I hope Susanna Kearsley has more of this up her sleeve. I’ll definitely be reading another of her novels soon to find the answer to that question.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15889463088982721682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1654601533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1654601533" />
    <a title="Celia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30261451-celia"><img alt="Celia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466854747p2/30261451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1654601533?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celia" href="/user/show/30261451-celia">Celia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12273538-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30261451-celia?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30261451-celia?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30261451-celia?shelf=group-bom">group-bom</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1654601533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13817870369724229768">The Rose Garden, by Susanna Kearsley is historical fiction. It is time travel. It is romance. It has a twist I did not see coming.<br/><br/>Eva Ward's beloved sister has died and she returns to their summer home in England to distribute Katrina's ashes. Strange things start to happen while she is staying at Trelowarth, resting and attempting to recover from her grief. She is transported back to the early 1700's to the Trelowarth of that time. She meets the Butlers and their best friend Fergal. She has no </span>
  <span id="freeText13817870369724229768" style="display:none">The Rose Garden, by Susanna Kearsley is historical fiction. It is time travel. It is romance. It has a twist I did not see coming.<br /><br />Eva Ward's beloved sister has died and she returns to their summer home in England to distribute Katrina's ashes. Strange things start to happen while she is staying at Trelowarth, resting and attempting to recover from her grief. She is transported back to the early 1700's to the Trelowarth of that time. She meets the Butlers and their best friend Fergal. She has no control over her teleportation. Makes for some interesting situations when she shows up unbid in modern clothes. <br /><br />The Butlers are smugglers and Daniel is a Jacobite. I had heard the term Jacobite in other books I have read. I now understand them to be a group that desired to restore the Roman Catholic Stuart King James II of England and Ireland . The sitting King, George, was not too pleased with that (!) and he and his followers considered them traitors worthy of death.<br /><br />The story alternates between present day in which plans to open a tearoom and garden tour are underway and the past, where Eva falls for Daniel.<br /><br />Lots of tie-ins between past and present. The writing coherently transposed between the two time periods. I am not the biggest fan of historical fiction romance so my rating reflects that.<br /><br />Better than a 3 but close enough to give it a 4. I will hazard a guess that if you do like romance, you will consider this book very good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13817870369724229768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_290157253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290157253" />
    <a title="Parvathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy"><img alt="Parvathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425840439p2/4915009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290157253?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parvathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parvathy" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy">Parvathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">time travel fiction lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Parvathy by: </span>
      Lekshmi Priya
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=fantasy-politics">fantasy-politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=movie-material">movie-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=historicals">historicals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=informative">informative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=past-lives">past-lives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=expected-more">expected-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=broken-characters">broken-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=feel-good">feel-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290157253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4169454479027681573">Where to begin? If you have read a Susanna Kersley's book before you would know that she writes her stories in dual time. You have the present where the story begins and the past where the actual story takes place and she will find one way or the other to get you there. In Winter Sea she brought us to the past by introducing a character who had the memories of one of her ancestors, in Marianna it was reincarnation and in the Rose Garden there is actual time travel to the past. Now why exactly on</span>
  <span id="freeText4169454479027681573" style="display:none">Where to begin? If you have read a Susanna Kersley's book before you would know that she writes her stories in dual time. You have the present where the story begins and the past where the actual story takes place and she will find one way or the other to get you there. In Winter Sea she brought us to the past by introducing a character who had the memories of one of her ancestors, in Marianna it was reincarnation and in the Rose Garden there is actual time travel to the past. Now why exactly only the main character and some other character seems to suffer from this particular problem is not sufficiently explained even though the author did mention something about a calling and need that is so great that it transcends time. That combined with the corresponding geographical location VOILA!! you have instant time travel. So there is Eva losing her sister and best friend Katrina to some illness in the present. Who travels to Trelowarths, a place where she and her sister spent time in their childhood, to scatter her ashes. While staying at Trelowarths Eva gets transported to the past to the year 1715 where she meets Danial Butler a smuggler who lived at Trelowarths at that time. Boy meets Girl and the story takes on...Of course this book cannot be classified as straight romance as there is a lot of history thrown in to the mix, which is highly accurate.<br /><br />In all the Susanna Kearsley book I have read the past is always centered around the failed Jacobite revolution of 1715. Even though each and every one of the protogonist does not suffer a sad ending due to the same it nevertheless does not amount to a satisfying read knowing that all the planning and preparation is going for a failed cause( that is if you are a fan of happy endings). In fact I think this book along with the two books mentioned above should be termed as series reads because the background for the story is same, only the characters and places differ. The same formula borders on to predictabilty that one suffers only when one is acquainted with the author's other works. As a stand alone novel The Rose Garden is an interesting read. The author has a gift with words that helps to create vivid images for the reader. The descriptions are endless and detailed about every other irrelevant thing in this book except the description of the main character. Even now after finishing the book I still don't know what the main character Eva looks like. Was she tall? What was the color of her hair? her eyes?. The author leaves this entirely up to the readers discretion but frankly I found it very difficult to read on without having any idea about whom to place in the scenarios. The character development was good although unbelievable at times. The truth is, it is hard to believe that both the characters have fallen head over heels in love only after a few encounters. I don't think there were enough exchanges between them to warrent such an outcome and that too when Daniel Butler was supposedily suffering from the lose of his beloved wife. On the whole The Rose Garden is a fascinating read if you have not much experience with the author's other novels. Even then it does not fall short of a good read. I would recommend this book to people who are in to time travel fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4169454479027681573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2393536748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8294514438468364418"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529853031i/25846930._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"When I meet a wind I cannot fight , I can do naught but set my sails to let it take me where it will."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>I enjoyed this one. It was not my favorite of her books that I've read, but I loved it just the same. There was a bit of time travel in this one. A great escape book. I think I would have liked a little more character development, but I suppose it would have made the story too long. Having been to Cornwall recently, I really enjoyed the setting, it brought back so many lovely memori</span>
  <span id="freeText8294514438468364418" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529853031i/25846930._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"When I meet a wind I cannot fight , I can do naught but set my sails to let it take me where it will."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I enjoyed this one. It was not my favorite of her books that I've read, but I loved it just the same. There was a bit of time travel in this one. A great escape book. I think I would have liked a little more character development, but I suppose it would have made the story too long. Having been to Cornwall recently, I really enjoyed the setting, it brought back so many lovely memories. It is definitely a place I'd like to return to. <br><br></span>

    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1640163-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327656830p2/1640163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2323537874?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/1640163-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402258589" href="/book/show/10836066-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1640163-candace?shelf=2018-5-star">2018-5-star</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2323537874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2181450655489128823">Eva Ward returns to the Cornish coast to scatter her sister's ashes. Trelowarth House, in the village of Polgelly, Cornwall, is a place filled with summer, childhood memories with the Hallett children Mark and Susan. Agreeing to do the public relations for the Hallett's roses and the future teahouse, she is wrapped up in the work, until one day she fades through centuries to appear in the early eighteenth century. She meets Daniel Butler, a free-trader who supports the Jacobite cause. She fades </span>
  <span id="freeText2181450655489128823" style="display:none">Eva Ward returns to the Cornish coast to scatter her sister's ashes. Trelowarth House, in the village of Polgelly, Cornwall, is a place filled with summer, childhood memories with the Hallett children Mark and Susan. Agreeing to do the public relations for the Hallett's roses and the future teahouse, she is wrapped up in the work, until one day she fades through centuries to appear in the early eighteenth century. She meets Daniel Butler, a free-trader who supports the Jacobite cause. She fades again reappearing in her own era. <br /><br />Eva discovers she can randomly fade between 1715 and the present and back again. When Eva is with Daniel, they develop feelings for each other. Eva is falling in love with Daniel. Will she be able to have a relationship with him when she can't control the time-travel? Can Eva save Daniel and his brother, Jack, from the failed Jacobite cause? What about her own century? Can she hide the evidence of her time-travel?<br /><br />This is my first book by Susanna Kearsley. The time-travel is accomplished with ley lines. I have encountered this same theory in other novels, so I didn't find it hard to believe it possible in this story. The characters, both primary and secondary, were well written and fleshed out. The plot is well thought out. The description is fabulous. I recommend this book to all who like time-travel. <br /><br />I have two favorite quotes I wish to share.<br /><br /><i>"When I meet a wind I cannot fight," he (Daniel) said, "I can do naught but set my sails to let it take me where it will."</i><br /><br /><i>Trelowarth," he (Daniel) countered, "is rooms gathered under a roof, nothing more." He refilled his cup and my own. "I argue 'tis never the place, but the people one shares it with who are the cause of our happiest memories. That is why we find that having lived them once, we can never recapture them.</i> (331)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2181450655489128823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9111437020757784883">In all honesty, I didn't think I was going to like this book at first. It started promising, but then just kept dragging on and on and ooonnnn with flowery descriptions and melancholy reminiscences until I wanted to scream, "Get <i>on with it!</i>"<br/><br/>But then, right around chapter 8, things finally started getting interesting. Once I'd made it to chapter 10 or so, I couldn't put it down. It won't be everyone's cup of tea, but I love time travel stories and this one hits the mark pretty well. My favorite c</span>
  <span id="freeText9111437020757784883" style="display:none">In all honesty, I didn't think I was going to like this book at first. It started promising, but then just kept dragging on and on and ooonnnn with flowery descriptions and melancholy reminiscences until I wanted to scream, "Get <i>on with it!</i>"<br /><br />But then, right around chapter 8, things finally started getting interesting. Once I'd made it to chapter 10 or so, I couldn't put it down. It won't be everyone's cup of tea, but I love time travel stories and this one hits the mark pretty well. My favorite characters were Daniel and Claire, and the twist at the end is just completely cool. I can't even really find words to describe it. Just...neat. This book made my night. I hope it makes yours.</span>

<div id="review_1205171222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1205171222" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1205171222?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=historical-fiction-alternatehistory">historical-fiction-alternatehistory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1205171222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12929798259596520719">I didn’t have to read much of this to realise that Susanna Kearsley’s work is going to be the perfect replacement for the comfort reading I got all the way through in the last two or three years (Mary Stewart’s romance/adventures). It has the same sense of place, the beautiful descriptions of landscape, and the same sort of heroine: female, curious, about to be swept up in bigger events than she’d ever have expected. And better: this is explicitly fantastical, where most of Mary Stewart’s books </span>
  <span id="freeText12929798259596520719" style="display:none">I didn’t have to read much of this to realise that Susanna Kearsley’s work is going to be the perfect replacement for the comfort reading I got all the way through in the last two or three years (Mary Stewart’s romance/adventures). It has the same sense of place, the beautiful descriptions of landscape, and the same sort of heroine: female, curious, about to be swept up in bigger events than she’d ever have expected. And better: this is explicitly fantastical, where most of Mary Stewart’s books were more mysteries, sometimes with hints at fantasy.<br /><br />And better again, whew, we don’t have first cousins getting married at the end.<br /><br />It does start off with kind of a slow pace, and Eva is only rarely involved in actual action, despite the backdrop of free trading and other such types of derring-do. And it is indeed a romance, so the ending is a happy one for most of the characters (though there’s a sadder note, too, with Eva’s sister’s husband; I was glad there was some closure at the end of story with him as well, even if it was a sadder story), and there’s plenty of romance going on — not just for Eva, but in the background. And yeah, I think Fergal and Daniel take the time travelling woman a little too lightly. They’re curious, but not curious enough to feel realistic. They both just decide to protect her right away.<br /><br />But I enjoyed it anyway: it has a great atmosphere, and the writing flows well. It’s a bit like The Time Traveler’s Wife, I guess, in that I wouldn’t want to examine how the timeline works too closely lest it fall apart, but it was the ideal fluff, and it had enough substance that I cared about the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12929798259596520719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_187331173" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187331173" />
    <a title="Misfit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit"><img alt="Misfit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496595931p2/1375548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187331173?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misfit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misfit" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit">Misfit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=time-slip">time-slip</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187331173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8952583181802672550">Recently divorced and at loose ends in life, Eva Ward accepts the task of scattering her dead sister’s ashes at their childhood home in Cornwall. Eva settles in for a long stay at Trelowarth house, but in true Kearsley fashion things start going bump in the night – and Eva is walking a path in the present one moment and the is next she’s stepped into the past – 1715 to be exact. She’s soon involved up to her neck with brothers Daniel and Jack Butler, Both smugglers like any good Cornishman, but </span>
  <span id="freeText8952583181802672550" style="display:none">Recently divorced and at loose ends in life, Eva Ward accepts the task of scattering her dead sister’s ashes at their childhood home in Cornwall. Eva settles in for a long stay at Trelowarth house, but in true Kearsley fashion things start going bump in the night – and Eva is walking a path in the present one moment and the is next she’s stepped into the past – 1715 to be exact. She’s soon involved up to her neck with brothers Daniel and Jack Butler, Both smugglers like any good Cornishman, but they’re also plotting with the Jacobites and things get a bit complicated at times…<br /><br /><i>“It was not the best of places I could be.”</i><br /><br />So as not to spoil I won’t reveal anymore, but fans of Kearsley should enjoy this a lot. This was a nice blend of time travel, romance, mystery and political intrigues. The time travel is handled nicely and is believable, although there was an unexpected twist at the end that took me by surprise – not 100% sure if I bought into that one. I liked watching the relationship grow between Eva and Daniel, but at the same time I didn’t find as much sizzle off the page chemistry I’d normally like to see. This is a book best to cuddle up with on a quiet weekend alone, and I mistakenly read it mid-week when my concentration wasn’t at its best. My bad. Kearsley fans will love this to bits, but while I enjoyed this it wasn’t quite up to par with The Winter Sea. 4/5 stars.<br /><br />Many thanks to Sourcebooks for an advance copy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8952583181802672550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_274902776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274902776" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3413113-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409063300p2/3413113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274902776?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3413113-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781402258596" href="/book/show/12806059-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274902776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15492311729418999078">I would really have loved to give this 3.5 stars.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.theultimatebooknook.blogspot.com'>www.theultimatebooknook.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>After reading The Winter Sea, I knew I had to read more by that author, so I picked this book up.<br/><br/>I wanted to love it as much as I did The Winter Sea but sadly I didn't. It was still enjoyable and very well written, it just didn't have the enchantment that The Winter Sea did.<br/><br/>Kearsley is a fantastic writer. She brings you into these worlds and makes you feel them. She can bring out so many emotions in just one boo</span>
  <span id="freeText15492311729418999078" style="display:none">I would really have loved to give this 3.5 stars.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theultimatebooknook.blogspot.com">www.theultimatebooknook.blogspot.com</a><br /><br />After reading The Winter Sea, I knew I had to read more by that author, so I picked this book up.<br /><br />I wanted to love it as much as I did The Winter Sea but sadly I didn't. It was still enjoyable and very well written, it just didn't have the enchantment that The Winter Sea did.<br /><br />Kearsley is a fantastic writer. She brings you into these worlds and makes you feel them. She can bring out so many emotions in just one book. You are sad, then happy and in love. You laugh and cry and feel every moment of the story. Very few authors can do that.<br /><br />Once again, Kearsley found a way to weave past and present together in an incredible way. It amazes me, the inventiveness she uses to put these stories together. Just like with the other book, I was much more into the past's story line than the present's. It is probably the hopeless romantic in me, since this is where the love story happens. <br /><br />The Rose Garden sagged a little in the middle. I found myself skimming parts trying to find where the story was going to pick up again. But, the plot twist at the end made up for that. I just felt the ending was too rushed. I wanted to know more. I wanted the loose ends to be tied up a bit better. I can't say much without giving parts of the story away but if you read it, I'm sure you will understand.<br /><br />In the end it was a good book, just a bit disappointing. I wanted more out of the story.<br />I will be reading more by Ms. Kearsley, though. I can't wait to see what else she has in store for me.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15492311729418999078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melodie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melodie" href="/user/show/5788507-melodie">Melodie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402258589" href="/book/show/10836066-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5788507-melodie?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5788507-melodie?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220242631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1853429524056792972"> Romance,historical fiction,fantasy? All genres fit this story. A young woman grieving the death of her sister finds comfort in the rambling old house on the Cornish coast, full of happy memories of summers past.<br/> All is not as it seems though, as Eva finds herself hopscotching between the present and the distant past of the 1700s. In the present,she is helping her childhood friends hang on to the family estate fallen on hard times. In the past she is introduced to the early residents, Daniel and</span>
  <span id="freeText1853429524056792972" style="display:none"> Romance,historical fiction,fantasy? All genres fit this story. A young woman grieving the death of her sister finds comfort in the rambling old house on the Cornish coast, full of happy memories of summers past.<br /> All is not as it seems though, as Eva finds herself hopscotching between the present and the distant past of the 1700s. In the present,she is helping her childhood friends hang on to the family estate fallen on hard times. In the past she is introduced to the early residents, Daniel and Jack Butler and their friend Fergal. There she is caught up in the world of smugglers, free traders as they call themselves. Romance, danger and high seas adventure combine to leave Eva's head spinning as she tries to maintain her grip on her senses.<br /> I found the story engaging and the characters easy to like or dislike as the case may be. I liked the fact the Eva's time travel was unpredictable and frequently inconvenient. This led to some terrific humor that only added to the strength of the story.I appreciate the way this author spins her story web,leaving the reader happily encased til the story's end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1853429524056792972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12162391746406952379">Four stars because for whatever reason, this was exactly the book I needed to read right now. Like, I wasn't really into the romance at all, but the writing worked for me, and I just enjoyed myself.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358145906?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emmy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emmy" href="/user/show/4838520-emmy">Emmy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781617932885" href="/book/show/25020346-the-rose-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838520-emmy?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838520-emmy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838520-emmy?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4838520-emmy?shelf=18th-century">18th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358145906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3349490853645269156"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413122968ra/11468465.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That twist! Brilliant! And so cleverly done. I didn't see it coming at all, but the foundation for it had been subtly built throughout the book without my noticing at all. It all just fit so seamlessly into the story. You know when some detail of a book so obviously sets up some plot point later in the book? This was the opposite!<br/><br/>I could have wished for the ending to be a bit more flushed out (I love a good reunion scene), but other than that, this was well written, intriguing, character-driven,</span>
  <span id="freeText3349490853645269156" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413122968ra/11468465.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That twist! Brilliant! And so cleverly done. I didn't see it coming at all, but the foundation for it had been subtly built throughout the book without my noticing at all. It all just fit so seamlessly into the story. You know when some detail of a book so obviously sets up some plot point later in the book? This was the opposite!<br><br>I could have wished for the ending to be a bit more flushed out (I love a good reunion scene), but other than that, this was well written, intriguing, character-driven, and unpredictable. Since this was my first Kearsley I didn't know whether a happy ending was inevitable, so I was more anxious than usual during the last 20%, but that just made it more suspenseful and exciting. <br><br>Time travels are usually hit or miss for me, but this was a different take on it since Eva traveled back and forth throughout the book rather than being stuck in one time period. I would say the majority of the book took place in the present and I loved the scenes from the past, so I could have spent hours longer on that, but small quibble. When you love a book, don't you always wish there was more? <br><br>Can't wait for my next Kearsley!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3349490853645269156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
